The genimages script in this directory uses GraphicsMagick to produce
a large collection of TIFF files (5568 files!) based on a sample input
file.  The TIFF files include the common varieties as well as many
esoteric varieties.  The TIFF files vary based on data organization
and bit/sample sizes.  For the moment, we produce uncompressed
('none'), rle, lzw, zip, zstd, and lzma compressed variants by default.

A "Q32" build of GraphicsMagick (e.g. --with-quantum-depth=32) is
recommended in order to write true 32-bit deep images, although a
common "Q16" build should be able to do everything (although not being
able to produce true 32-bit data samples), and even a "Q8" build of
GraphicsMagick is able to read most of the generated files.

Many applications will be unable to read many of the generated TIFF
files.

The script is not integrated into the GraphicsMagick test framework so
some editing may be desireable, such as to use a special
GraphicsMagick build or to use your favorite input image.

Some patience is required while generating an image containing 65536 colors!

Generated intermediate files are named like "master_*" and final
output files are named like "img_*".  Such files can safely be removed
(e.g. "rm master_* img_*").  If parameters are changed which influence
generation of the master files, the "master_*" files should be removed
since they are not re-generated if they already exist.

A handy way to quickly view the many generated files on an X11 display is:

  gm display -delay 3 img*.tif

These files are currently generated (as shown in the summary.txt file
generated by the script):
